Clarifying the Temporal Reference in the Hadith
Defining temporal reference and critiquing two views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the 'future' in the hadith is relative to Adam's state, not the speaker's present, and the critique of interpretations that lose specificity.

Core Idea
The hadith's 'future' is relative to Adam's state, not our time.

The commentator begins by resolving a potential confusion: the 'future' mentioned in the hadith does not refer to the time of the Prophet's speech, but to the time when Adam was between water and clay. This sets the stage for evaluating two competing interpretations and their theological shortcomings.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the opening lines carefully. Notice how the commentator first defines 'future' in relation to the time indicated by the context.
The passage uses technical terms like 'استقبال' and 'تعبير عن المتحقق'.
2
Understand the more apparent interpretation
The commentator presents the view that the hadith is a rhetorical device emphasizing certainty, like using the past tense for a future event.
3
Examine the second interpretation and its objection
Some say the hadith means prophethood was preordained in eternal knowledge. But the commentator objects that this loses the specific virtue for Muhammad, as all things are known to God eternally.
This objection applies to both interpretations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( في أنه تعبير عن المتحقق إلخ) لا يخفى أن المراد بالاستقبال هو الاستقبال بالنسبة إلى الزمان الذي دل الكلام على وقوع المعبر عنه فيه وهذا مشترك بين المشبه والمشبه به فلا أن الاستقبال في المشبه بالنسبة إلى زمان التكلم ولا كذلك في المشبه به . أعني الحديث النبوي بل الاستقبال فيه بالنسبة إلى كون آدم عليه السلام بين الماء والطين. والأظهر أن يقال : في أنه تعبير عن غير المتحقق في زمان بما يدل على تحققه في ذلك الزمان تنبيهاً على القطع واليقين بتحققه هذا وقيل : معنى الحديث كون نبوته عليه السلام مقدورة في الأزل وثابتة في العلم الإلهي الأزلي. وهذا غير ما ذكره الشارح لكن يرد عليه أنه لا يناسب تقييده بقوله : وآدم الماء والطين إذ يرد على كل من التوجهين أن سياق الحديث يشعر باختصاصه عليه السلام بين بهذه الفضيلة من بين الأنبياء صلوات الله عليهم وعلى كل من التوجهين لا اختصاص للفضيلة المذكورة به عليه السلام لأن نبوّة كل نبي بل كل حال لكل أحد ثابت في العلم الإلهي الأزلي، ويجوز التعبير عن كل حال علم وقوعه في المستقبل بما يدل على تحققه قبل وقوعه بما ذكره . والأقرب أن يقال في معنى الحديث للكل بحسب مرتبة كل منهم عليهم السلام عند تعيناتهم العمائية، لما سيرد عليهم من النشآت المتواردة وأحكامها ونبينا عليه السلام كان في نشأته الروحانية نبياً للأرواح ومتوسطاً في تعيين حصص كمالاتهم الروحانية التي بحسبها يظهر كمالاتهم الجسمانية، كما يروى عنه عليه السلام أول ما خلق الله نوري، هو المفهوم من شرح : الجندي رحمه الله .
His saying: (that it is an expression of what is realized etc.) It is not hidden that the intended meaning of 'future' is future relative to the time which the speech indicates the occurrence of what is expressed, and this is common between the similes and the object of comparison. So it is not that the future in the first is relative to the time of speaking, nor similarly in the second, i.e., the prophetic hadith. Rather the future in it is relative to the state of Adam (peace be upon him) being between water and clay. The more apparent is to say: it is an expression of something not realized at a time by what indicates its realization at that time, alerting to the certainty and conviction of its realization. This is what is said. And it was said: the meaning of the hadith is that his prophethood (peace be upon him) was preordained in eternity and established in the eternal divine knowledge. This is different from what the commentator mentioned, but it is objected that it does not suit its restriction by his saying 'and Adam between water and clay', for both approaches are subject to the objection that the context of the hadith suggests his (peace be upon him) particular distinction with this virtue among the prophets (blessings of God upon them). And on both approaches there is no particularity of the mentioned virtue to him (peace be upon him) because the prophethood of every prophet, nay every state of every individual, is established in the eternal divine knowledge, and it is permissible to express every state whose occurrence in the future is known by what indicates its realization before its occurrence as mentioned. The closest is to say in the meaning of the hadith: for each according to the rank of each of them (peace be upon them) at their 'ama'iyyah determinations, due to what will come upon them of successive emergences and their rulings. And our Prophet (peace be upon him) was in his spiritual emergence a prophet to the spirits and a mediator in determining the shares of their spiritual perfections by which their bodily perfections appear, as is narrated from him: 'First of what God created is my light.' This is understood from the commentary of al-Jundī (may God have mercy on him).
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is an exegetical gloss on a phrase from the main text: 'in that it is an expression of what is realized in the future with a past tense.' The commentator clarifies that the 'future' in the hadith 'I was a prophet while Adam was between water and clay' is relative to the time when Adam was between water and clay, not relative to the speaker's present. The most apparent interpretation is that it is a rhetorical expression emphasizing certainty, like using the past tense for a future event. Another interpretation says the hadith means that his prophethood was preordained in eternity. The commentator rejects this because it would not be specific to Prophet Muhammad, as all prophets' prophethood is known in eternity. The closest interpretation is that the hadith refers to each prophet's rank in the 'ama'iyyah determinations, and our Prophet was a prophet to spirits and a mediator. The gloss concludes by referencing a narration 'First of what God created is my light' and a commentary by al-Jundī.

Key Terms
استقبال
تعبير عن المتحقق
العلم الإلهي الأزلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith means the Prophet literally existed as a person before Adam.
Correction: The commentator clarifies it is a rhetorical expression of certainty, not literal pre-existence.

Checkpoint
What is the primary objection the commentator raises against both interpretations?
A) They contradict the Quran
B) They do not uniquely distinguish the Prophet Muhammad
C) They are grammatically incorrect
D) They imply anthropomorphism

Key Takeaway
The hadith's virtue requires an interpretation that is unique to Muhammad, which neither simple certainty nor eternal knowledge provides.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the hadith 'I was a prophet while Adam was between water and clay,' do you feel a deeper awe for the Prophet's status, or do you pass over it as a familiar phrase? How can you renew your appreciation for his unique role in light of this lesson's critique that the hadith must convey a virtue exclusive to him?
?
Consider your own beliefs about divine destiny: do you ever use God's foreknowledge as an excuse for passivity? This lesson shows that even the Prophet's preordination is a specific honor, not a generic fact. How does that challenge your understanding of God's will in your life?
?
The commentator faults interpretations that fail to highlight Muhammad's distinct excellence. In what areas of your life do you treat the Prophet's teachings as generic wisdom rather than uniquely authoritative commands? What would change if you took his exclusive prophethood more seriously?

Prophethood

The Preferred Interpretation: Spiritual Prophethood in 'Ama'iyyah Determinations
Presenting the preferred exegesis involving spiritual pre-creation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the final, preferred interpretation that the hadith refers to the Prophet's spiritual prophethood among souls in the realm of 'ama'iyyah determinations.

Core Idea
The hadith speaks of prophetic ranks in the spiritual realm of 'ama'iyyah.

After rejecting two inadequate explanations, the commentator presents the closest interpretation: the hadith refers to each prophet's rank in their 'ama'iyyah determinations — a subtle spiritual pre-creation state. Here, our Prophet was a prophet to spirits and the mediator of spiritual perfections, aligning with the famous hadith 'First of what God created is my light.'

Guided Path
1
Read the final Arabic segment
Start with 'والأقرب أن يقال' and read to the end. Notice how it introduces a new concept: 'تعينات عمائية'.
This term refers to a state of being before physical creation.
2
Understand the concept of 'ama'iyyah determinations
Each prophet has a rank in this pre-physical realm. The Prophet Muhammad's role there was to be a prophet to spirits and a distributor of spiritual perfections.
3
Connect to the 'light' hadith
The commentator references 'First of what God created is my light' to support this interpretation.
This shows continuity with a well-known tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( في أنه تعبير عن المتحقق إلخ) لا يخفى أن المراد بالاستقبال هو الاستقبال بالنسبة إلى الزمان الذي دل الكلام على وقوع المعبر عنه فيه وهذا مشترك بين المشبه والمشبه به فلا أن الاستقبال في المشبه بالنسبة إلى زمان التكلم ولا كذلك في المشبه به . أعني الحديث النبوي بل الاستقبال فيه بالنسبة إلى كون آدم عليه السلام بين الماء والطين. والأظهر أن يقال : في أنه تعبير عن غير المتحقق في زمان بما يدل على تحققه في ذلك الزمان تنبيهاً على القطع واليقين بتحققه هذا وقيل : معنى الحديث كون نبوته عليه السلام مقدورة في الأزل وثابتة في العلم الإلهي الأزلي. وهذا غير ما ذكره الشارح لكن يرد عليه أنه لا يناسب تقييده بقوله : وآدم الماء والطين إذ يرد على كل من التوجهين أن سياق الحديث يشعر باختصاصه عليه السلام بين بهذه الفضيلة من بين الأنبياء صلوات الله عليهم وعلى كل من التوجهين لا اختصاص للفضيلة المذكورة به عليه السلام لأن نبوّة كل نبي بل كل حال لكل أحد ثابت في العلم الإلهي الأزلي، ويجوز التعبير عن كل حال علم وقوعه في المستقبل بما يدل على تحققه قبل وقوعه بما ذكره . والأقرب أن يقال في معنى الحديث للكل بحسب مرتبة كل منهم عليهم السلام عند تعيناتهم العمائية، لما سيرد عليهم من النشآت المتواردة وأحكامها ونبينا عليه السلام كان في نشأته الروحانية نبياً للأرواح ومتوسطاً في تعيين حصص كمالاتهم الروحانية التي بحسبها يظهر كمالاتهم الجسمانية، كما يروى عنه عليه السلام أول ما خلق الله نوري، هو المفهوم من شرح : الجندي رحمه الله .
His saying: (that it is an expression of what is realized etc.) It is not hidden that the intended meaning of 'future' is future relative to the time which the speech indicates the occurrence of what is expressed, and this is common between the similes and the object of comparison. So it is not that the future in the first is relative to the time of speaking, nor similarly in the second, i.e., the prophetic hadith. Rather the future in it is relative to the state of Adam (peace be upon him) being between water and clay. The more apparent is to say: it is an expression of something not realized at a time by what indicates its realization at that time, alerting to the certainty and conviction of its realization. This is what is said. And it was said: the meaning of the hadith is that his prophethood (peace be upon him) was preordained in eternity and established in the eternal divine knowledge. This is different from what the commentator mentioned, but it is objected that it does not suit its restriction by his saying 'and Adam between water and clay', for both approaches are subject to the objection that the context of the hadith suggests his (peace be upon him) particular distinction with this virtue among the prophets (blessings of God upon them). And on both approaches there is no particularity of the mentioned virtue to him (peace be upon him) because the prophethood of every prophet, nay every state of every individual, is established in the eternal divine knowledge, and it is permissible to express every state whose occurrence in the future is known by what indicates its realization before its occurrence as mentioned. The closest is to say in the meaning of the hadith: for each according to the rank of each of them (peace be upon them) at their 'ama'iyyah determinations, due to what will come upon them of successive emergences and their rulings. And our Prophet (peace be upon him) was in his spiritual emergence a prophet to the spirits and a mediator in determining the shares of their spiritual perfections by which their bodily perfections appear, as is narrated from him: 'First of what God created is my light.' This is understood from the commentary of al-Jundī (may God have mercy on him).
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is an exegetical gloss on a phrase from the main text: 'in that it is an expression of what is realized in the future with a past tense.' The commentator clarifies that the 'future' in the hadith 'I was a prophet while Adam was between water and clay' is relative to the time when Adam was between water and clay, not relative to the speaker's present. The most apparent interpretation is that it is a rhetorical expression emphasizing certainty, like using the past tense for a future event. Another interpretation says the hadith means that his prophethood was preordained in eternity. The commentator rejects this because it would not be specific to Prophet Muhammad, as all prophets' prophethood is known in eternity. The closest interpretation is that the hadith refers to each prophet's rank in the 'ama'iyyah determinations, and our Prophet was a prophet to spirits and a mediator. The gloss concludes by referencing a narration 'First of what God created is my light' and a commentary by al-Jundī.

Key Terms
تعينات عمائية
الصورة النورانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred interpretation, what does the hadith primarily describe?
A) The Prophet's prophethood in the eternal divine knowledge
B) The Prophet's role as a prophet to spirits in the spiritual realm
C) The creation of Adam's body
D) The Prophet's appointment as a messenger after Adam

Key Takeaway
The Prophet Muhammad's unique prophetic role began in the spiritual realm of 'ama'iyyah, making him a prophet to spirits before physical creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Timing of Miracles: Preceding vs. Following Claim
Sanusi distinguishes miracles before and after the claim, and rules on short delays.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between a miracle preceding the claim of prophethood and one following it, and how a short delay affects its indicativeness.

Core Idea
A miracle shortly after the claim indicates truth; one shortly before does not.

Before examining the details of delayed miracles, Sanusi clarifies the basic temporal relationship between a miracle and the claim of prophethood. He distinguishes miracles that occur before the claim from those that occur after, and then considers the case of a short delay. This passage sets the stage for the more complex discussion of extended delays.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the key terms: معجز متقدم and معجز متأخر.
2
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: a miracle preceding the claim and one following it. For each, note the ruling regarding its indication of truth.
Pay attention to the phrase 'بزمان يسير يعتاد مثله' (by a short time customarily similar).
3
Contrast the rulings
Contrast the ruling for a preceding miracle with that for a following one. Why does a preceding miracle not indicate truth at all, while a following one does? Think about the conditions of prophethood.
The key difference is that a preceding miracle happens before the claimant is known as a prophet, so it cannot be tied to the claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهذا الذي قررناه إنما هو ( في ( المعجز ( المتقدم) على الدعوى ( وأما المتأخر) عنها ( فإما ) أن يكون تأخره ) بزمان يسير يعتاد مثله فظاهر أنه دل على الصدق بخلاف المتقدم بزمان يسير فإنه لا يدل عليه أصلاً ( وإما ) أن يكون تأخره ) بزمان متطاول مثل أن يقول : معجزتي أن يحصل كذا بعد شهر فحصل فاتفقوا على أنه (معجز دال على ثبوت النبوة لكن اختلفوا في وجه دلالته ( فقيل: إخباره عن الغيب فيكون ( المعجز على هذا القول ( مقارناً ) للدعوى لكن تخلف عنها علمنا بكونه معجزاً ( وإنما انتفى التكليف بمتابعته حينئذ ) أي لم يجب على الناس التصديق بنبوته ومتابعته في الزمان الواقع بين الإخبار وحصول الموعود به لأن شرطه أي شرط التكليف بالتصديق والمتابعة العلم بكونه معجزاً) وذلك إنما يحصل بعد وجود ما وعد به ( وقيل حصوله أي حصول الموعود به ( فيكون) المعجز على هذا القول ( متأخراً) عن الدعوى ( وقيل : يصير قوله ) أي إخباره معجزاً عند حصوله أي حصول الموعود به ( فيكون) المعجز على هذا القول ( متأخراً) باعتبار صفته أعني كونه معجزاً ) والحق أن المتأخر) هو (علمنا بكونه معجزا) يعني أن المختار هو القول الأول لأن إخباره كان إخباراً بالغيب في نفس الأمر فيكون معجزاً مقارناً للدعوى، والمتخلف عنها هو علمنا بكونه معجزاً لا كونه معجزاً فبطل بذلك القول الثالث، وأما القول الثاني فلا طائل تحته لأن ذلك الحصول لا يمكن جعله معجزاً إلا إذا كان خارقاً للعادة وربما لم يكن كذلك وإن جعل شرطاً لاتصاف الأخبار بالإعجاز فقد رجع إلى الثالث وبطل ببطلانه ولهذا لم يوجد هذا القول في أبكار الأفكار مر قوله : ( لأن شرطه العلم بكونه معجزاً) فيه بحث وهو أنه مخالف ما مر في بحث النظر من أن وجوب النظر على المكلف لا يتوقف على النظر وعلى العلم بوجوبه وإلا لدار وذلك لأن العلم بكونه معجزاً إنما يكون بعد النظر، فالصواب أن يقال : لأن شرطه التمكن من العلم يكونه معجزاً وذلك إنما يحصل بعد وجود ما وعد به .
So this which we have established is only concerning the miracle preceding the claim. As for the one following it, either its delay is by a short time customarily similar, then it is apparent that it indicates truth, unlike the preceding by a short time, for it does not indicate truth at all. Or its delay is by an extended time, like if he says: my miracle is that such-and-such will happen after a month, and it happens, then they agreed that it is a miracle indicating the establishment of prophethood, but they differed concerning the aspect of its indication. One said: his informing of the unseen, so the miracle on this view is simultaneous with the claim, but our knowledge of it being a miracle lags behind it. And the obligation of following him is waived at that time, i.e., people are not obliged to believe in his prophethood and follow him in the period between the informing and the occurrence of the promised thing, because its condition, i.e., the condition of the obligation of belief and following, is knowledge that it is a miracle, and that only occurs after the existence of what was promised. And another said: its occurrence, i.e., the occurrence of the promised thing, so the miracle on this view is delayed from the claim. And another said: his statement, i.e., his informing, becomes a miracle at its occurrence, i.e., the occurrence of the promised thing, so the miracle on this view is delayed in terms of its attribute, namely its being a miracle. And the truth is that the delayed thing is our knowledge that it is a miracle, meaning that the chosen view is the first one, because his informing was an informing of the unseen in itself, so it is a miracle simultaneous with the claim, and what lags behind is our knowledge of it being a miracle, not its being a miracle. Thus the third view is invalidated. As for the second view, there is no substance to it, because that occurrence cannot be made a miracle unless it is extraordinary, and perhaps it is not so; and if it is made a condition for the description of the informing with miraculousness, then it reverts to the third view and is invalidated by its invalidation. Hence this view is not found in Abkar al-Afkar. Note: his saying: 'because its condition is knowledge that it is a miracle' contains a discussion: it contradicts what was stated in the discussion of reasoning that the obligation of reasoning upon the accountable person does not depend on reasoning or on knowledge of its obligation, otherwise there would be a circle, because knowledge that it is a miracle only comes after reasoning. So the correct statement is: because its condition is the ability to know that it is a miracle, and that only occurs after the existence of what was promised.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage discusses the timing of miracles relative to the claim of prophethood. It distinguishes between a miracle that precedes the claim (mutaqaddim) and one that follows it (muta'akhkhir). For a preceding miracle, if it occurs exactly at the time of the claim or shortly before, it indicates truth, but if it occurs too early (e.g., in childhood), it does not indicate prophethood because the conditions of prophethood are not yet present. For a delayed miracle, the author considers two scenarios: a short delay (customarily similar) and a long delay (e.g., a month). For a long delay, scholars agree it is a miracle indicating prophethood, but they differ on how it indicates. The first opinion: the miracle is the informing of the unseen itself, so it is simultaneous with the claim, but our knowledge of it is delayed; thus the obligation to follow does not apply until after the promised event. The second opinion: the miracle is the actual occurrence of the promised event, so it is temporally delayed. The third opinion: the informing becomes a miracle at the time of occurrence, so the miracle is delayed in attribute. The author chooses the first opinion, arguing that the informing is a miracle in itself (being a report of the unseen), and only our knowledge lags. The second opinion is rejected because the occurrence may not be extraordinary, and if it is made a condition, it reduces to the third opinion which is invalid. The gloss at the end clarifies a subtle point: the condition for obligation is not knowledge itself but the ability to attain knowledge after reasoning, avoiding circularity.

Key Terms
معجز متقدم
معجز متأخر
بزمان يسير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that any miracle close to the claim, whether before or after, is equally indicative. But the author distinguishes based on temporal order relative to the claim.
Correction: A miracle before the claim is not tied to the claim and thus cannot serve as proof of prophethood, while one after the claim is directly connected.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a miracle that occurs a short time after the claim of prophethood?
A) It does not indicate truth at all
B) It indicates truth
C) It indicates truth only if it is extraordinary
D) Its indication depends on the type of miracle

Key Takeaway
A miracle shortly after the claim indicates the truth of the claim, but one shortly before does not.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you seek Allah's guidance through istikhara, do you look for signs before or after making the decision? How does Sanusi's distinction challenge you to check the timing of your signs? What will you change starting today?
?
Have you ever taken a past blessing (e.g., a dream, a coincidence) as confirmation for a current choice without checking whether it preceded or followed your intention? How will you apply this lesson to ensure your evidence is valid?
?
If Allah sends a clear sign after you commit to a good deed, do you recognize it as confirmation? Or do you doubt and look for more? Write one commitment to trust the signs that follow your sincere claim.

Three Opinions on Delayed Miracles with Long Delay
Sanusi enumerates three opinions on how a delayed miracle indicates prophethood and argues for the first.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three scholarly opinions on how a delayed miracle with a long delay indicates prophethood, and why the author chooses the first opinion.

Core Idea
The informing itself is the miracle, not the event it promises.

When a miracle is promised to occur after an extended period, scholars agree it is a miracle but differ on how it indicates prophethood. Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani presents three views: that the miracle is the informing itself, that it is the actual occurrence, or that the informing becomes a miracle at the time of occurrence. He then defends the first view, refuting the others. This passage delves into the precise nature of miraculousness and its relation to human knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, noting the three opinions introduced by 'فقيل', 'وقيل', and 'وقيل'. Pay attention to the author's critique and final choice.
2
Identify each opinion
List the three opinions: (1) the informing of the unseen is the miracle, (2) the occurrence is the miracle, (3) the informing becomes a miracle at the occurrence. Understand the implications of each.
The author labels them 'فقيل', 'وقيل', 'وقيل'.
3
Analyze the author's argument
Read the part beginning 'والحق أن المتأخر...' where the author chooses the first opinion and refutes the others. Note the reasons: the third is invalid because the informing was a miracle in itself; the second has no substance because the occurrence may not be extraordinary.
The author also notes a circularity issue in a gloss at the end, but that is a separate point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

So this which we have established is only concerning the miracle preceding the claim. As for the one following it, either its delay is by a short time customarily similar, then it is apparent that it indicates truth, unlike the preceding by a short time, for it does not indicate truth at all. Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the miracle is the physical event that occurs later, but the author argues that the informing itself is the miracle.
Correction: The miracle is the act of foretelling the unseen, which is a form of khabar al-ghayb; the event merely confirms that the report was miraculous.

8 min
The Timing of Miracles: Three Opinions and the Correct View
Enumeration and refutation of three opinions on miracle timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three classical opinions on the timing of miracles relative to the claim of prophethood and the reasoning behind the correct view.

Core Idea
The miracle is simultaneous with the claim; only our knowledge of it is delayed.

In this passage, the author examines a key question in the theology of prophethood: when exactly does a miracle occur in relation to the prophet's claim? Three opinions are debated, and the correct view is defended. As you read, pay attention to the distinction between the miracle itself and our knowledge of it—a subtle but crucial point.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Let the author's structure sink in.
The author uses a concise, argumentative style.
2
Identify the three opinions
Look for the phrases 'قيل' and 'وقيل' to spot the first and second opinions. The third is introduced with 'وقيل' as well. Notice how each opinion relates the miracle to the claim.
3
Understand the correct view and refutation
The author states 'والحق أن المتأخر هو علمنا بكونه معجزا'. See why the other two opinions fail: the third is invalid because it confuses the miracle with our knowledge, and the second is baseless because the promised thing may not be superordinary.
The refutation relies on the nature of the report as a prophecy of the unseen.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this distinction matters: it preserves the immediacy of the miracle as a sign, while acknowledging that human recognition may come later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الأول - المقصد الثاني : في حقيقة المعجزة . الناس التصديق بنبوته ومتابعته في الزمان الواقع بين الإخبار وحصول الموعود به لأن شرطه أي شرط التكليف بالتصديق والمتابعة العلم بكونه معجزاً) وذلك إنما يحصل بعد وجود ما وعد به ( وقيل حصوله أي حصول الموعود به ( فيكون) المعجز على هذا القول ( متأخراً) عن الدعوى ( وقيل : يصير قوله ) أي إخباره معجزاً عند حصوله أي حصول الموعود به ( فيكون) المعجز على هذا القول ( متأخراً) باعتبار صفته أعني كونه معجزاً ) والحق أن المتأخر) هو (علمنا بكونه معجزا) يعني أن المختار هو القول الأول لأن إخباره كان إخباراً بالغيب في نفس الأمر فيكون معجزاً مقارناً للدعوى، والمتخلف عنها هو علمنا بكونه معجزاً لا كونه معجزاً فبطل بذلك القول الثالث، وأما القول الثاني فلا طائل تحته لأن ذلك الحصول لا يمكن جعله معجزاً إلا إذا كان خارقاً للعادة وربما لم يكن كذلك وإن جعل شرطاً لاتصاف الأخبار بالإعجاز فقد رجع إلى الثالث وبطل ببطلانه ولهذا لم يوجد هذا القول في أبكار الأفكار
The First Observatory - Second Objective: On the Reality of the Miracle. People [must] believe in his prophethood and follow him in the time between the report and the occurrence of the promised thing because its condition—i.e., the condition of obligation to believe and follow—is knowledge of its being a miracle, and that only occurs after the existence of what was promised. And it was said: its occurrence i.e., the occurrence of the promised thing, so the miracle, according to this opinion, is delayed after the claim. And it was said: his word—i.e., his report—becomes a miracle at its occurrence i.e., the occurrence of the promised thing, so the miracle, according to this opinion, is delayed with respect to its attribute, namely its being a miracle. And the truth is that what is delayed is our knowledge of its being a miracle, meaning that the chosen [opinion] is the first because his report was a report of the unseen in itself, so it was a miracle concurrent with the claim, and what lags behind it is our knowledge of its being a miracle, not its being a miracle. Thus the third opinion is invalidated. As for the second opinion, there is no substance to it because that occurrence cannot be made a miracle unless it is superordinary, and perhaps it is not so. And if it is made a condition for the description of the report with miraculousness, then it returns to the third and is invalidated by its invalidity. Hence this opinion is not found in Abkār al-Afkār.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the timing of the miracle relative to the claim of prophethood. It presents three opinions: First, that the miracle occurs after the promised thing, so the obligation to believe begins only after that. Second, that the promised thing itself is the miracle, so it occurs after the claim. Third, that the prophecy becomes miraculous at the occurrence of the promised thing, so the miracle is delayed in its attribute. The correct view is that the miracle is simultaneous with the claim—since the prophecy of the unseen is itself the miracle—but our knowledge of its miraculousness is delayed. Thus the third opinion is invalid, and the second is baseless because the promised thing may not be superordinary.

Key Terms
معجزة
توقيت
دعوى النبوة
الموعود به
العلم بكونه معجزاً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The miracle itself occurs after the claim of prophethood.
Correction: The miracle is simultaneous with the claim; our knowledge of its miraculousness is what is delayed.

Checkpoint
According to the correct view, what is actually delayed in relation to the miracle?
A) The miracle itself
B) The claim of prophethood
C) Our knowledge of the miracle
D) The occurrence of the miracle

Key Takeaway
The miracle is concurrent with the claim of prophethood; only our recognition of it is delayed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The lesson teaches that the miracle is concurrent with the claim, but our knowledge lags. Is there an area of your faith where you are waiting for certainty before acting, while the truth is already present? What step can you take today to act on what you already know is true?

The Ash'ari View: Miracles Indicate Truthfulness by Custom, Not Rational Necessity
Author argues that miracles indicate prophetic truthfulness only by custom, not by rational necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ash'ari theologians consider miracles to have only customary indication of prophetic truthfulness, rather than rational or scriptural indication.

Core Idea
Miracles prove prophethood only because God customarily links them to truthful claims.

In this passage, the author clarifies the nature of the proof provided by miracles. Some argued that miracles rationally necessitate the truthfulness of a prophet, like an effect implies a cause. But the Ash'ari position is more nuanced: miracles alone are not inherently proof; they only gain significance when combined with a claim of prophethood and a challenge, due to God's customary practice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the rhythm of the argument come through before you interpret.
Notice the author's direct rejection of two alternatives before affirming his own.
2
Identify the two rejected alternatives
The passage explicitly rejects rational indication (like an act shows an agent) and scriptural indication (circular). Find these and understand why each is dismissed.
Rational indication is rejected because miracles can occur without prophecy (end times, saintly marvels). Scriptural indication would require already accepting the prophet.
3
Understand the basis for customary indication
The author affirms that miracles indicate truthfulness only by custom (ʿādah). This means God has established a pattern: when a miracle coincides with a claim of prophethood and a challenge, it signals truth.
This is the core Ash'ari position, distinct from rationalist views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البحث الثالث في كيفية دلالتها على صدق مدعي النبوة، وهذه الدلالة ليست دلالة عقلية محضة كدلالة الفعل على وجود الفاعل ودلالة أحكامه وإتقانه على كونه عالماً بما صدر عنه، فإن الأدلة العقلية ترتبط لنفسها بمدلولاتها ولا يجوز تقديرها غير دالة عليها وليست المعجزة كذلك فإن خوارق العادات كانقطاع السماوات وانتثار الكواكب وتدكك الجبال يقع عند تصرم الدنيا وقيام الساعة ولا إرسال في ذلك الوقت، وكذلك تظهر الكرامات على أيدي الأولياء من غير دلالة على صدق مدعى النبوة ولا دلالة سمعية لتوقفها على صدق النبي فيدور بل هي دلالة عادية كما أشار إليه بقوله : (وهي عندنا أي الأشاعرة ... ) قوله : ( وليست المعجزة كذلك فإن خوارق العادات إلخ ) هذا رد على الشيخ ومتابعيه فإنه هو القائل بأن دلالة المعجزة عقلية كما سيذكره الآن، وقد يجاب عنه : بأن الشيخ إنما يعتبر الدلالة العقلية بعد القيود أعني المقارنة لدعوى النبوة والتحدي فلا يتجه حينئذ قوله : فإن خوارق العادات إلخ، فتأمل.
The Third Discussion: On How It Indicates the Truthfulness of the Claimant of Prophethood. This indication is not a purely rational indication, like the indication of an act upon the existence of an agent and the indication of its precision and perfection upon him being knowledgeable about what issued from him. For rational evidences are intrinsically linked to their implications and cannot be supposed non-indicative. The miracle is not like that, for superordinary events such as the splitting of the heavens, the scattering of stars, and the crumbling of mountains occur at the end of the world and the establishment of the Hour, and there is no mission at that time. Likewise, marvels (karāmāt) appear at the hands of saints without indicating the truthfulness of a claimant of prophethood. Nor is it a scriptural indication, because that depends on the truthfulness of the prophet, which would be circular. Rather, it is a customary indication, as he indicated by his saying: 'It is with us, i.e., the Ash'aris...' His saying: 'The miracle is not like that, for superordinary events...' is a refutation of al-Shaykh and his followers, for he is the one who says that the indication of the miracle is rational, as he will mention now. And it may be answered: that al-Shaykh only considers rational indication after restrictions, i.e., conjunction with the claim of prophethood and challenge, so then his saying 'for superordinary events...' does not apply. So reflect.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is the third discussion on how miracles prove the truthfulness of a prophet. The view is that the indication is not purely rational (like the argument from design) because miracles can occur in non-prophethood contexts (e.g., final hour events or saintly marvels) and thus are not intrinsically tied to prophecy. Nor is it scriptural, because that would require prior acceptance of the prophet's truthfulness. Instead, it is a customary indication (dalāla ʿādiyya): God has established a custom that when a miracle accompanies a claim of prophethood along with a challenge, it verifies the claim. The commentator notes that this is a response to those (like al-Shaykh) who consider the indication rational, but the counter-response is that the rational indication is considered only after adding the conditions of challenge and claim, so the objection does not hold.

Key Terms
دلالة عقلية
دلالة عادية
خوارق العادات
كرامات
تحدي
دعوى النبوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That miracles are inherently and universally proof of prophethood regardless of context.
Correction: Miracles alone are not proof; they indicate truthfulness only when accompanied by a claim of prophethood and a challenge, and only due to God's customary practice.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari view in this passage, what kind of indication do miracles have for verifying prophethood?
A) Rational (ʿaqliyya)
B) Scriptural (samʿiyya)
C) Customary (ʿādiyya)
D) Both rational and scriptural

Key Takeaway
Miracles indicate prophetic truthfulness only because God's custom ties them to truthful claims when accompanied by a challenge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If miracles are not rationally necessary proofs, but only customary signs from God, does your trust in the prophethood of Muhammad (ﷺ) rely on the miraculous Qur'an as a challenge? Reflect on whether you have ever questioned the strength of that proof when faced with doubts.
?
When you witness extraordinary events in the world or in the lives of pious people, do you automatically assume they confirm some spiritual status? How does this lesson's distinction between miracles and saintly marvels change the way you interpret such events?
?
The lesson ends with 'so reflect.' What personal attachment do you have to the idea that faith must be based on rationally undeniable proofs? Could your faith withstand the Ash'ari view that it is ultimately based on God's custom and your own response to that custom?

Spiritual Pleasure as a Prophetic Sign
Presentation of spiritual pleasure as a prophetic sign with scriptural evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that spiritual pleasure is one of the three types of prophetic signs, evidenced by the Prophet's experience of divine nourishment.

Core Idea
The prophet's spiritual nourishment replaces physical food as a sign.

This passage begins by describing the inner state of the prophet, who is turned toward God. It explains that he experiences spiritual pleasures through holy lights that substitute for physical sustenance, as confirmed by a hadith. This is the first type of prophetic sign: an internal, spiritual miracle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on spiritual pleasure
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice how the author describes the spiritual pleasure as taking the place of food.
The hadith quoted is well-known.
2
Analyze the evidence
Identify the hadith used as proof. Ask: how does this show a sign of prophethood?
3
Connect to the broader classification
Understand that this is the first of three types presented. Reflect on why spiritual states are considered miraculous.
This guards against the misconception that only physical acts are miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المتوجه فيوجد فيه من اللذات الروحانية بالأنوار القدسية ما يقوم مقام الغذاء كما أشير إليه بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام أبيت عند ربي يطعمني ويسقيني وأما القول فكالأخبار بالغيب وسببه ما مر في المقصد الأول من الانجذاب نفسه النقية عن الشواغل البدنية إلى الملائكة السماوية وانتقاشها بما فيها من الصور وانتقال الصورة إلى المتخيلة والحس المشترك وأما الفعل فبأن يفعل فعلا لا نفي غيره من نتق جبل أو شق بحر وقد تقدم بيانه بأن نفسه لقوتها تتصرف في مادة العناصر كما تتصرف في أجزاء بدنه
As for the one turned [toward God], there are found in him spiritual pleasures through holy lights that take the place of nourishment, as alluded to by his saying, peace be upon him: 'I spend the night with my Lord; He feeds me and gives me drink.' As for speech, it is like news of the unseen, and its cause is what was mentioned in the first investigation: the attraction of the soul, pure from bodily distractions, to the celestial angels, and its impression with the forms they contain, and the transfer of the form to the imagination and common sense. As for action, it is that he performs an act that is not beyond [ordinary] like uprooting a mountain or splitting a sea; and its explanation has already been given: that his soul, due to its strength, acts upon the matter of the elements just as it acts upon the parts of his body.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage classifies the signs of prophethood into three categories. The first is the inner state of the prophet himself, who experiences spiritual pleasures that substitute for physical nourishment, as indicated by the hadith where the Prophet says he is fed and watered by his Lord. The second is speech: miracles of informative nature, such as predicting future events, which originate from the prophet's pure soul receiving forms from angels. The third is action: extraordinary physical acts like moving mountains or splitting seas, which stem from the power of the prophet's soul controlling material elements. The author explains the cause for each: for speech, it is the attraction of the soul to the celestial world; for action, it is the soul's domination over matter.

Key Terms
اللذات الروحانية
الأنوار القدسية
الغذاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are only physical events like healing or controlling nature.
Correction: Spiritual experiences, such as the prophet's divine sustenance, are also valid signs of prophethood.

Checkpoint
What does the hadith 'I spend the night with my Lord; He feeds me and gives me drink' illustrate?
A) The prophet never needed to eat
B) Spiritual pleasures can replace physical food
C) Angels brought food to the prophet
D) The prophet was always fasting

Key Takeaway
Spiritual pleasure, as experienced by the Prophet, is a genuine prophetic sign that demonstrates divine support.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt truly satisfied by an act of worship or closeness to Allah, to the point that your physical desires faded? What would it take for you to seek that spiritual nourishment more than your daily bread?
?
The Prophet ﷺ said he is fed and given to drink by his Lord during the night. When you are in hardship or hunger, do you turn to Allah as your ultimate sustainer, or do you rely only on material means? Will you make a sincere du'a tonight asking Allah to feed your soul?
?
If spiritual pleasures are real and can replace physical needs, why do you still chase after worldly comforts while neglecting the 'holy lights' available through worship? What is one distraction you can remove this week to make space for that spiritual experience?

Speech: News of the Unseen as a Prophetic Sign
Explanation of speech (news of the unseen) as a prophetic sign with its cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how prophetic speech—news of the unseen—is a second type of miracle, originating from the soul's connection to angels.

Core Idea
Prophetic news of the unseen comes from the soul's pure reception from angels.

This lesson focuses on the second type of prophetic sign: speech. The author explains that the prophet's ability to foretell future events arises from his soul's attraction to the celestial angels. The soul, purified from bodily distractions, receives forms from the angels and transmits them to the imagination and common sense, resulting in true predictions.

Action: Physical Miracles as Prophetic Signs
Explanation of physical miraculous actions as a prophetic sign with illustration of cause.

Physical miracles occur when the prophet's soul controls matter directly.

Mu'tazila Objection and Sheikh's Response on Miracle Indication
Mu'tazila objection and first Ash'ari response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila objection that a miracle on a liar is impossible in God's wisdom, and the Ash'ari response that a miracle has a definite indication of truthfulness, making it impossible to occur on a liar.

Core Idea
A miracle's definite indication of truthfulness makes it impossible to occur on a liar.

The Mu'tazila argue that while God can create a miracle on a liar, His wisdom prevents it because it would be misleading. The Ash'ari scholar al-Shaykh and his followers respond by asserting that a miracle by definition carries a definite indication of truthfulness, so it cannot be divorced from that meaning. This lesson examines both positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila objection
Read the first part of the passage where the Mu'tazila state their view. Note their distinction between power and wisdom.
They say it is possible in power but impossible in wisdom.
2
Understand the wisdom objection
The Mu'tazila argue that creating a miracle on a liar would imply his truthfulness, which is misguidance and thus ugly for God to do.
3
Read the Sheikh's response
Read the second part where Ash-Shaykh and some companions argue that a miracle has a definite indication of truthfulness, making it impossible on a liar.
They claim it is not possible in itself, not just in wisdom.
4
Analyze the logical alternatives
Notice the two alternatives: if the miracle indicates truth, then the liar would be truthful (impossible); if it does not indicate truth, then it is divorced from its essential indication (also impossible).
Either way, a miracle on a liar leads to contradiction.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالت المعتزلة : خلق المعجز على يد الكاذب) مقدور لله تعالى لعموم قدرته، لكنه ( ممتنع ) وقوعه في حكمته ) لأن فيه إيهام صدقه وهو إضلال قبيح من الله فيمتنع صدوره عنه كسائر القبائح ( قال الشيخ وبعض أصحابنا : إنه ) أي خلق المعجزة على يد الكاذب ( غير مقدور) في نفسه ( لأن لها أي للمعجزة ( دلالة على الصدق قطعاً) أي دلالة قطعية يمتنع التخلف فيها ( فلا بد لها من وجه دلالة ) إذ به يتميز الدليل الصحيح عن غيره ( وإن لم نعلمه أي ذلك الوجه (بعينه فإن دل) المعجز المخلوق على يد الكاذب على الصدق كان الكاذب صادقاً) وهو محال ) وإلا انفك ( المعجز ( عما يلزمه ) من دلالته القطعية على مدلوله وهو أيضا محال ( وقال القاضي : اقتران ظهور المعجزة بالصدق ( ليس أمراً لازماً لزوماً عقلياً كاقتران وجود الفعل بوجود فاعله بل ( هو أحد العاديات ( كما عرفت ( فإذا جوزنا انخراقها ) أي انخراق العاديات ( عن مجراها ( العادي ( جاز إخلاء المعجز عن اعتقاد الصدق وحينئذ يجوز إظهاره على يد الكاذب) إذ لا محذور فيه سوى خرق العادة في المعجزة والمفروض أنه جائز ( وأما بدون ذلك ) التجويز ( فلا يجوز إظهاره على يده لأن العلم بصدق الكاذب محال تذنيب من الناس من أنكر إمكان المعجزة ) في نفسها ( ومنهم من أنكر (دلالتها على صدق مدعي النبوة ( ومنهم من أنكر العلم بها وستأتيك ) في المقصد التالي لهذا المقصد ) شبههم بأجوبتها ) . ( قوله : ( لأن العلم بصدق الكاذب محال حاصل الكلام أن عادة اقتران المعجزة بالصادق وعدم جواز خرق العادة فيها يستلزم الصدق وصدق الكذب محال وكذا عادة خلق العلم يستلزم العلم بصدق الكاذب، وبهذا التقرير يظهر اندفاع تخيل أن اعتقاد الشيء قطعاً لا يستلزم وقوعه وأما كون الاعتقاد مطابقاً فما لا مدخل فيه للجعل حتى يقال أنه أيضاً عادي.
The Mu'tazila said: creating a miracle at the hand of a liar is within God's power due to His universal power, but its occurrence is impossible in His wisdom, because it involves suggesting his truthfulness, which is an ugly misguidance from God, so it is impossible for it to occur from Him like all ugly things. (Ash-Shaykh and some of our companions said: it—i.e., creating a miracle at the hand of a liar—is not possible in itself, because the miracle has a definite indication of truthfulness, i.e., a definite indication from which deviation is impossible. So it must have a mode of indication, by which a correct proof is distinguished from others, even if we do not know that mode in particular. For if a miracle created at the hand of a liar indicates truthfulness, then the liar would be truthful, which is impossible; otherwise, the miracle would be divorced from what it entails, of its definite indication of its implicatum, which is also impossible.) (And al-Qadi said: the conjunction of a miracle's appearance with truthfulness is not a necessary conjunction intellectually like the conjunction of the existence of an act with the existence of its agent, but rather it is one of the customary matters, as you have learned. So if we allow the breach of these customs from their usual course, it becomes permissible for the miracle to be divested of the belief in truthfulness, and then it becomes permissible to manifest it at the hand of a liar, since there is no objection other than breaching custom in the miracle, and it is assumed that it is permissible. But without that permission, it is not permissible to manifest it at his hand, because knowledge of a liar's truthfulness is impossible.) (Appendix: among people are those who denied the possibility of the miracle in itself, and among them are those who denied its indication of the truthfulness of the claimant of prophethood, and among them are those who denied knowledge of it; and their doubts along with their answers will come to you in the next aim.) (His saying: 'Because knowledge of a liar's truthfulness is impossible.' The gist of the discussion is that the custom of the conjunction of the miracle with the truthful person and the impermissibility of breaching custom therein necessitates truthfulness, and the truthfulness of a liar is impossible. Similarly, the custom of creating knowledge necessitates knowledge of the liar's truthfulness. By this formulation, the illusion that certain belief in something does not necessitate its occurrence is dispelled. As for the belief being in conformity, there is no room for artifice in it such that it could be said that it is also customary.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer discussion. First, the Mu'tazila objection: creating a miracle on a liar is possible in power but impossible in wisdom because it would be misguidance. Then two Ash'ari responses. The first response (from Ash-Shaykh and some companions) argues that a miracle has a definite indication of truthfulness, so it cannot occur on a liar because that would entail the impossible. The second response (from al-Qadi) argues that the connection is customary, not rational, so if we allow breach of custom, it could occur on a liar, but without that it is impossible. The passage ends with an appendix (tadhnib) listing three types of deniers of miracles. Then a marginal note explains the phrase 'knowledge of a liar's truthfulness is impossible' by clarifying that custom necessitates truthfulness, and certain belief does not require actual occurrence.

Key Terms
معجزة
دلالة قطعية
ممتنع في الحكمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Ash'ari view is that miracles are impossible on liars simply because of divine wisdom, similar to the Mu'tazila.
Correction: The Sheikh's response shows that the impossibility is logical, not just based on wisdom: a miracle's definite indication of truthfulness cannot coexist with a liar.

Checkpoint
According to the Sheikh's response, why is a miracle impossible on a liar?
A) Because God's wisdom prevents it.
B) Because it has a definite indication of truthfulness that would lead to contradiction.
C) Because miracles are only for prophets.
D) Because it would be a breach of custom.

Key Takeaway
A miracle's definite indication of truthfulness logically precludes its occurrence on a liar, as it would entail contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mu'tazila believed God would not allow a miracle on a liar because it would be misguidance. Have you ever trusted someone based on a seeming sign from God, only to be deceived? How does this lesson's distinction between power and intrinsic impossibility protect you from being misled by impressive signs? Will you commit to verifying truth through the Prophet's authentic message rather than emotional experiences?
?
If a miracle has a definite indication of truth, then the Prophet's miracles are absolutely certain proofs of his truthfulness. Does your heart truly rest in that certainty, or do you entertain doubts raised by skeptics? What concrete action can you take today to strengthen your conviction in the Messenger's truth, such as studying his miracles or reflecting on the Quran's inimitability?
?
The Ash'ari argue that a liar cannot perform a true miracle because it would entail a contradiction. When you face confusion about which teacher or claim to follow, do you assess their 'signs' against the decisive proofs of the Prophet? Will you commit to using the standard of the Quran and Sunnah to evaluate all claims of guidance, even those that appear miraculous?

Al-Qadi's Customary View and Deniers of Miracles
Al-Qadi's customary view and appendix on deniers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Qadi's argument that the link between a miracle and truthfulness is customary, not rational, and his solution allowing miracles on liars by breaching custom, along with the appendix listing three types of deniers.

Core Idea
The miracle-truth link is customary, so breach of custom allows miracles on liars.

Al-Qadi provides a different response: the conjunction of a miracle with truthfulness is a matter of custom (ʿāda) rather than rational necessity. If we allow breach of custom, a miracle could appear on a liar without indicating truth. The passage ends with an appendix listing three groups who deny miracles in different ways, and a marginal note clarifying the impossibility of knowing a liar's truthfulness.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Qadi's argument
Read the part beginning with 'Wa-qāla al-qāḍī'. Note his distinction between rational and customary connections.
He compares it to the necessary link between act and agent.
2
Understand the conditional
If we allow breach of custom, the miracle can be divested of belief in truthfulness, so it can appear on a liar. Without that, it is impossible because knowledge of a liar's truthfulness is impossible.
3
Review the appendix (tadhnīb)
Read the part listing three groups who deny miracles: those denying possibility, those denying indication, and those denying knowledge of them.
The author promises to address their doubts later.
4
Consider the marginal note
Read the note explaining that custom necessitates truthfulness and dispels the illusion that certain belief does not require actual occurrence.

?

?

?

Be honest: have you ever doubted that a clear sign from God actually points to truth? Use al-Qadi's emphasis on custom to strengthen your conviction, and take a step to reinforce your faith in God's signs.

Ash'ari Proof and Philosophers' View on Prophethood
Jurjani presents the Ash'ari proof and the philosophers' view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari argument that the actual occurrence of Muhammad's prophethood proves its possibility, and the philosophers' alternative claim that prophethood is rationally necessary for the perfection of the cosmic system.

Core Idea
What happened is possible; what is needed for order is necessary.

Jurjani begins by establishing the Ash'ari proof for the possibility of prophethood: because we know through revelation that Muhammad was a prophet, we know that prophethood is possible. He then contrasts this with the philosophers' view, who argue that prophecy is rationally necessary because the perfect order of the universe requires a prophet to establish laws of justice. Let's examine these two foundational positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Ash'ari argument
Focus on the phrase 'وحجتنا فيه إثبات نبوة محمد له فإن الدال على الوقوع دال على الإمكان'. Note the logical move: actual occurrence implies possibility.
The Ash'ari do not need to prove possibility separately; the fact of Muhammad's prophethood suffices.
2
Understand the philosophers' claim
Read the philosophers' statement: prophethood is rationally necessary for the most perfect system that eternal providence demands. Ask yourself: what is the basis of this necessity?
The philosophers rely on the concept of a providentially ordered cosmos.
3
Compare the foundations
Contrast the two approaches: Ash'ari rely on revealed occurrence, philosophers on rational necessity. Notice how each starts from different premises.
This comparison sets the stage for the broader debate on the nature of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الأول - المقصد الثالث : في إمكان البعثة ( في إمكان البعثة وحجتنا فيه إثبات نبوة محمد له فإن الدال على الوقوع دال على الإمكان ) بلا اشتباه ( وقالت الفلاسفة : إنها واجبة عقلا لما مر من النظام الأكمل الذي تقتضيه العناية الأزلية لا يتم بدون وجود النبي الواضع لقوانين العدل ) وقال بعض المعتزلة : يجب على الله و ) فصل (بعضهم ) فقال : ( إذ علم الله من أمته أنهم يؤمنون ) وجب عليه إرسال النبي إليهم لما فيه من استصلاحهم ( وإلا ) أي وإن لم يعلم ذلك بل علم أنهم لا يؤمنون لم يجب الإرسال بل (حسن) قطعاً لأعذارهم ) وقال أبو هاشم يمتنع خلوه ) أي خلو البعث ) عن تعريف شرعيات لا يستقل العقل بها لأن البعثة الخالية عنه لا فائدة فيها ( وجوزه الجبائي لتقرير الواجبات العقلية فإنه فائدة جليلة (و) جوزه أيضاً (لتقرير الشريعة المتقدمة) سواء كانت مندرسة أولا ( وقيل : ( إنما يجوز البعث لتقريرها ( إذا اندرست وهو) أي هذا الذي نقلناه من المعتزلة على الوجوه المختلفة ( بناء ) أي مبني على أصلهم ) الفاسد أعني قاعدة التحسين والتقبيح العقليين وما يتفرع عليها من اعتبار الغرض الألطاف ورعاية الأصلح فيكون فاسداً أيضاً ، (و) على تقدير صحته (لا ووجوب
The first observatory - the third aim: on the possibility of prophethood. (On the possibility of prophethood: our proof for it is the establishment of the prophethood of Muhammad, peace be upon him, for what indicates occurrence indicates possibility) without confusion. (And the philosophers said: it is rationally necessary, due to the what has passed about the most perfect system that is required by eternal providence, which cannot be complete without the existence of the prophet who establishes the laws of justice.) And some Mu'tazila said: it is obligatory upon God—and (some) distinguished and said: (If God knows of His community that they will believe, then sending the prophet is obligatory upon Him, because of the setting them aright that it contains; otherwise (i.e., if He knows they will not believe), then sending is not obligatory, but rather good) to cut off their excuses. And Abu Hashim said: it is impossible for it (i.e., the prophethood) to be free from defining legal matters that reason cannot grasp independently, because a prophethood devoid of it has no benefit. And al-Jubbai permitted it for establishing rational duties, for it is a great benefit, and he also permitted it for establishing the previous sharia, whether it was forgotten or not. And it was said: prophethood is only permitted for establishing it when it has been forgotten. And this (which we have reported from the Mu'tazila in its different forms) is based on their corrupt principle, namely the principle of rational al-tahsin wa al-taqbih (good and evil), and what branches from it of considering purpose and favors and observing the most beneficial, so it is also corrupt. And even if it were accepted, it would not necessitate...
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage discusses the possibility of prophethood (ba'thah). The Ash'ari proof is that the actual occurrence of Muhammad's prophethood demonstrates possibility. Then it reviews various non-Ash'ari positions: the philosophers hold that prophethood is rationally necessary for the perfect system; the Mu'tazila have various views—some saying it is obligatory if God knows people will believe, otherwise good; Abu Hashim says it must include legal rulings not known by reason; al-Jubbai says it can also confirm rational duties and previous sharia. The passage ends with an Ash'ari critique: all these views are based on the corrupt principle of rational good and evil (tahsin wa taqbih aqli), which the Ash'aris reject.

Key Terms
بعثة
إمكان
نبوة محمد
فلاسفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Ash'ari deny that prophethood has any benefit or purpose.
Correction: The Ash'ari do not deny benefits; they only reject rational necessity and argue that God is not obligated by human notions of good and evil. The passage itself doesn't address this directly, but it sets the stage for later critique.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari argument in this passage, what establishes the possibility of prophethood?
A) Rational necessity
B) The actual occurrence of Muhammad's prophethood
C) The need for a perfect system
D) Consensus of scholars

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari prove the possibility of prophethood from its actual occurrence in Muhammad, while the philosophers argue it is rationally necessary for the perfection of the universe.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The philosophers argue that a prophet is rationally necessary for a just society. Do you live as if the Prophet's guidance is necessary for your daily life, or merely optional? When you face a moral decision, do you automatically turn to the Sunnah, or do you first rely on your own reason? Commit this week to consulting the Prophet's example before making one significant decision.
?
The Ash'ari proof takes the actual prophethood of Muhammad as a fact that cannot be denied. In your heart, do you sometimes treat the prophethood as just a historical fact, or does it carry the same weight of certainty that compels you to obey? Ponder: if you truly believe his occurrence proves his possibility, does that possibility translate into actual submission in your actions today?
?
The philosophers' system depends on 'eternal providence' requiring a prophet. But what if your personal life lacks this order? Are you actively seeking the prophetic model to bring justice and balance into your own affairs, or are you content with chaos? Ask yourself: what is one area of your life where you need the Prophet's law of justice, and what is one step you will take today to implement it?

Prophethood

Mu'tazila Views and the Ash'ari Critique
Jurjani details Mu'tazila positions on prophethood and critiques their rational foundation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various Mu'tazila positions on the obligation or goodness of sending prophets, and the Ash'ari critique that all these positions are based on the corrupt principle of rational good and evil.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila tie prophethood to rational obligation; Ash'aris reject their foundation.

In this passage, Jurjani reviews the diverse views of the Mu'tazila on prophethood. Some say God must send a prophet if He knows people will believe, otherwise it is merely good. Abu Hashim insists prophethood must include revealed laws beyond reason, while al-Jubbai allows it for confirming rational duties and previous sharia. The passage ends with a sharp Ash'ari critique: these opinions are all built on the principle of rational good and evil (tahsin wa taqbih), which the Ash'aris consider corrupt. Let's unpack each view and the critique.

Guided Path
1
List the Mu'tazila positions
Read the passage and identify each distinct Mu'tazila view: the general view that it is obligatory, the conditional view based on God's knowledge, the view of Abu Hashim, the view of al-Jubbai, and the view restricting it to when previous sharia is forgotten.
Notice how each position modifies the condition for sending a prophet.
2
Understand the basis of each view
For each view, ask: what purpose does sending a prophet serve? For Abu Hashim, benefit requires revealed rulings; for al-Jubbai, it confirms rational duties or revives forgotten sharia.
The underlying principle is that God acts for wise purposes, which the Ash'ari reject as binding on God.
3
Analyze the Ash'ari critique
Read the final part where Jurjani states that all these views are based on the corrupt principle of rational good and evil (التحسين والتقبيح العقليين). Understand why Ash'aris consider it corrupt: it subjects God to human reason.
The critique is that even if the principle were accepted, it would not lead to the conclusions claimed.

The first observatory - the third aim: on the possibility of prophethood. (On the possibility of prophethood: our proof for it is the establishment of the prophethood of Muhammad, peace be upon him, for what indicates occurrence indicates possibility) without confusion. (And the philosophers said: it is rationally necessary, due to the what has passed about the most perfect system that is required by eternal providence, which cannot be complete without the existence of the prophet who establishes the laws of justice.) And some Mu'tazila said: it is obligatory upon God—and (some) distinguished and said: (If God knows of His community that they will believe, then sending the prophet is obligatory upon Him, because of the setting them aright that it contains; otherwise (i.e., if He knows they will not believe), then sending is not obligatory, but rather good) to cut off their excuses. And Abu Hashim said: it is impossible for it (i.e., the prophethood) to be free from defining legal matters that reason cannot grasp independently, because a prophethood devoid of it has no benefit. And al-Jubbai permitted it for establishing rational duties, for it is a great benefit, and he also permitted it for establishing the previous sharia, whether it was forgotten or not. And it was said: prophethood is only permitted for establishing it when it has been forgotten. And this (which we have reported from the Mu'tazila in its different forms) is based on their corrupt principle, namely the principle of rational al-tahsin wa al-taqbih (good and evil), and what branches from it of considering purpose and favors and observing the most beneficial, so it is also corrupt. And even if it were accepted, it would not necessitate...
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage discusses the possibility of prophethood (ba'thah). The Ash'ari proof is that the actual occurrence of Muhammad's prophethood demonstrates possibility. Then it reviews various non-Ash'ari positions: the philosophers hold that prophethood is rationally necessary for the perfect system; the Mu'tazila have various views—some saying it is obligatory if God knows people will believe, otherwise good; Abu Hashim says it must include legal rulings not known by reason; al-Jubbai says it can also confirm rational duties and previous sharia. The passage ends with an Ash'ari critique: all these views are based on the corrupt principle of rational good and evil (tahsin wa taqbih aqli), which the Ash'aris reject.

الجبائي

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila deny that prophethood can be for simply confirming rational duties; they think it must always include new laws.
Correction: Al-Jubbai explicitly permits it for confirming rational duties, showing variation within the Mu'tazila.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Ash'ari critique of all the Mu'tazila views on prophethood?
A) They deny the possibility of prophethood altogether
B) They are based on the corrupt principle of rational good and evil
C) They ignore the role of miracles
D) They contradict the Quran

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila disagree on the conditions for sending a prophet, but all base their views on rational good and evil, which the Ash'aris reject as an invalid foundation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about God's sending of prophets, do you instinctively feel that God must do certain things for our benefit? Where does that expectation come from? Are you willing to surrender that assumption if it is not explicitly taught in revelation?
?
The Mu'tazila built their arguments on reason, but the Ash'aris say that foundation is corrupt. Examine your own beliefs: Do you rely more on logical reasoning or on scriptural texts when deciding what God must or must not do? How would you respond if someone told you that your reasoning imposes obligations on God?
?
This lesson shows that even within the Mu'tazila, there were disagreements about God's obligations. Have you ever felt that your own understanding of God's justice or mercy must be exactly as you imagine? How does the Ash'ari critique challenge you to humble your intellect before the sovereignty of God, accepting that He does as He wills without being subject to rational constraints?

Proof of Possibility from Actual Prophethood and Refutation
Al-Iji argues from actual prophethood to possibility, then refutes opposing views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Iji uses the actual occurrence of Muhammad's prophethood to prove the possibility of sending messengers, and how he refutes the objections of philosophers and Mu'tazila without denying their own principles.

Core Idea
Proven occurrence proves possibility; objections based on rational obligation do not refute general possibility.

This passage is a defense of the possibility of prophethood against both philosophers and Mu'tazila. Al-Iji first establishes a simple logical proof: because Muhammad was indeed a prophet, sending prophets is possible. He then presents and refutes various alternative theories that try to make prophethood either obligatory or contingent on God's knowledge of belief. The refutation hinges on distinguishing 'general possibility' from 'specific possibility', allowing him to sidestep their arguments while maintaining his own proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof from actuality
Start with the opening sentence: the fact that Muhammad was a prophet proves that prophethood is possible. Note the logical move from actuality to possibility.
2
Examine the philosophers' objection
Read how the philosophers claim prophethood is rationally obligatory for the perfect system. Ask: does this contradict possibility?
3
Understand the Mu'tazila distinctions
Go through the various Mu'tazila positions: some say obligatory, some make it conditional on God's knowledge, others discuss the need for religious law. See how they all assume rational obligation.
4
Identify al-Iji's refutation strategy
Notice that al-Iji says these views are based on the corrupt principle of rational beautification and vilification. Even if sound, they only affect specific possibility, not general possibility.
The key is the distinction between general and specific possibility.
5
Apply the distinction
Understand that al-Iji's claim is only general possibility, which is compatible with obligation. Therefore, the objections do not harm his proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في إمكان البعثة وحجتنا فيه إثبات نبوة محمد له فإن الدال على الوقوع دال على الإمكان بلا اشتباه وقالت الفلاسفة : إنها واجبة عقلا لما مر من النظام الأكمل الذي تقتضيه العناية الأزلية لا يتم بدون وجود النبي الواضع لقوانين العدل وقال بعض المعتزلة : يجب على الله و فصل بعضهم فقال : إذا علم الله من أمته أنهم يؤمنون وجب عليه إرسال النبي إليهم لما فيه من استصلاحهم وإلا وإن لم يعلم ذلك بل علم أنهم لا يؤمنون لم يجب الإرسال بل حسن قطعاً لأعذارهم وقال أبو هاشم يمتنع خلوه عن تعريف شرعيات لا يستقل العقل بها لأن البعثة الخالية عنه لا فائدة فيها وجوزه الجبائي لتقرير الواجبات العقلية فإنه فائدة جليلة و جوزه أيضاً لتقرير الشريعة المتقدمة سواء كانت مندرسة أولا وقيل : إنما يجوز البعث لتقريرها إذا اندرست وهو أي هذا الذي نقلناه من المعتزلة على الوجوه المختلفة بناء أي مبني على أصلهم الفاسد أعني قاعدة التحسين والتقبيح العقليين وما يتفرع عليها من اعتبار الغرض الألطاف ورعاية الأصلح فيكون فاسداً أيضاً و على تقدير صحته لا ووجوب يضرنا في مدعانا فإنا إنما ادعينا الإمكان العام الذي يجامع الوجوب لا الإمكان الخاص الذي ينافيه وغرضنا هنا رد شبه المنكرين للبعثة
On the possibility of sending a messenger. Our proof for it is establishing the prophethood of Muhammad, peace be upon him, for that which indicates occurrence indicates possibility without confusion. The philosophers said: It is rationally obligatory due to what has passed about the most perfect system that eternal providence requires, which is not completed without the existence of a prophet who establishes the laws of justice. Some Mu'tazila said: It is obligatory upon God. And some of them made a distinction: If God knows of His community that they will believe, sending the prophet to them is obligatory because of the reform in it. Otherwise, if He does not know that but knows that they will not believe, sending is not obligatory but rather good, definitely to cut off their excuses. Abu Hashim said: It is impossible for it to be free from defining religious matters that the intellect cannot independently grasp, because a sending that is free from that has no benefit. Al-Jubba'i allowed it for establishing rational obligations, for that is a great benefit, and he also allowed it for establishing the previous law, whether it was abrogated or not. And it was said: Sending is only permissible to establish it when it has been abrogated. And this which we have transmitted from the Mu'tazila in various ways is based on their corrupt principle, namely the basis of rational beautification and vilification and what branches from it concerning consideration of purpose, favors, and observing the most beneficial, so it is also corrupt. And even if it were sound, it does not harm us in our claim, for we only claim general possibility, which is compatible with obligation, not specific possibility that contradicts it. Our aim here is to refute the doubts of the deniers of the sending.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is a proof and refutation. It begins by stating the main proof: the actual occurrence of Muhammad's prophethood proves the possibility of sending prophets, because whatever exists is possible. Then it presents objections from three groups: (1) The philosophers: they say it is rationally obligatory, citing the need for a prophet to establish a perfect system. (2) Some Mu'tazila: they say it is obligatory upon God, with a distinction made by some: if God knows people will believe, sending is obligatory for reform; if not, it is only good. (3) Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i and others debated whether a prophet must bring new religious laws or simply confirm rational duties. Al-Iji then refutes these views by noting they are based on the corrupt Mu'tazili principle of rational beautification and vilification (التجسيم). Even if that principle were sound, it would not harm the author's claim, because he only argues for general possibility (الإمكان العام), which includes both necessity and possibility. The passage concludes by affirming that the goal is to refute the deniers of prophethood.

الفلاسفة

الإمكان العام
الإمكان الخاص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that proving possibility requires disproving every alternative theory about prophethood's necessity or contingency.
Correction: Al-Iji shows that the actual occurrence of Muhammad's prophethood is sufficient to prove general possibility, regardless of whether others claim it is necessary or conditional.

Checkpoint
What is al-Iji's main argument for the possibility of sending prophets?

B) The Mu'tazila say it is obligatory
C) The actual occurrence of Muhammad's prophethood proves it
D) It is known by rational intuition

Key Takeaway
Actual occurrence is the strongest proof of possibility; objections based on obligation or conditionality do not affect general possibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have I ever doubted the reality of prophethood because I overthink what God 'should' do? What would it mean for my faith to accept that the actual occurrence of Muhammad's prophethood is sufficient proof — without needing my intellectual approval first?
?
Al-Iji calls the Mu'tazili principle 'corrupt' because it imposes human standards of good and evil on God. In what area of my life am I still judging God's actions by what I think is 'fair' or 'best'? Will I surrender that judgment today?
?
The lesson says general possibility is compatible with obligation. Is there a truth in my faith that I resist because I feel it 'shouldn't be that way'? How can I train myself to first accept what God has actually done, before demanding it fit my expectations?
